(2) **`HUNTER_TELEGRAPH_COUNT` (9) feel** ‚Äî does the stroke-alpha pulse read as "unstable, shoot me now" in the seconds before a clump births a Hunter, or does it read as a new enemy class despite the no-color-shift design intent (¬ß2.5.1)? (3) **"How to Play" card legibility** (Options ‚Üí How to Play, ¬ß2.16) ‚Äî does the single static 1080√ó660 panel read at a glance, or does it need CS013 P3's clip-scroll fallback after all? **Prior session (CS014 P1):** implemented CS014 Phase 1 per ¬ß2.2 of `PLANNED-FEATURES-CS014.md` (FORK-B resolved: a dedicated **silent** surface ‚Äî no VoiceSys involvement, no Dan lines that round). Landed `HintSys`, a module alongside `AudioSys`/`MusicSys`/`VoiceSys`: eight adaptive one-shot onboarding hints (`shield`/`hook`/`dock`/`clump`/`birth`/`tow`/`thrust`/`decay`, in `TUT_IDS`'s dual role as id list + display-priority order), copy as DATA (`TUT_LINES`) with `{action}` placeholders resolving through the live `bindings` table at *draw* time via `tutKey()` (reusing the Controls screen's `prettyKey`, so a hint is rebind-safe by construction), a delay-never-drop re-arm rule (the deliberate inversion of VoiceSys's drop-not-queue ‚Äî a hint describes state that's still true, so a busy channel postpones rather than loses it), and a silent-latch veteran-skip (a demonstrated skill burns its hint with the same persisted `tutSeen` write and no display, latch pass running before the display pass). **One deliberate deviation from the phase prompt, spec-fidelity-preserving:** the prompt's `chainPrev`/`coalescedPrev` edge-detector fields were dropped as provably redundant once the re-arm rule forces the arms to be persistent state (`dock` arms on `chain.length > 0`, `birth` on `hunterCoalesced > 0` ‚Äî both already read elsewhere, so no dead state was added); behavior matches the spec exactly. **Playtest asks flagged, not yet actioned:** a first-run 90 s trace fired 7 of 8 hints back-to-back at the minimum `TUT_DUR`+`TUT_GAP` (9.5 s) spacing ‚Äî worth judging by eye for nagging, `TUT_GAP` is the knob if so; the `thrust` hint has a dead band (0.5‚Äì1.5 s held) where it neither shows nor latches; copy and `TUT_Y` (96) are unjudged look-calls. **A fixture hazard worth remembering for future long-running headless tests:** emptying `game.debris` triggers a real wave-clear ‚Üí `nextWave()` respawn, so an idle test ship can take a real hit and steal the hint channel from what the test meant to watch ‚Äî fixed with a `quiesce(inst)` helper (one immobile debris parked half a world away as a permanent wave-clear blocker). Tests: `scratchpad/test-cs014-p0.js` (110) + `scratchpad/test-cs014-p1.js` (99, drives the real `startGame`/`update`/`damageShip`/`saveSettings`), full regression green at 55 files/4,616 assertions at the time. **Prior session (CS013 P4):** implemented CS013 Phase 4 (Group C, ¬ß3 of `PLANNED-FEATURES-CS013.md`), the round's last phase, reading `STATUS.md` first as required. Re-grepped every anchor before editing (all confirmed at or near the planning doc's own estimates): `SHIELD_DRAIN`/`SHIELD_RECHARGE`/`SHIELD_HIT_COST`/`AUTO_SHIELD_SCORE_PENALTY` (L127‚Äì131), the ship init `this.shieldOn`/`this.energy` (L2804‚Äì2805), the passive-recharge `else`-branch (L2842‚Äì2844, confirmed the ONLY `SHIELD_RECHARGE` site via grep), the `invuln` decrement (L2875), the auto-shield branch's `s.invuln = HIT_STUN_DURATION` (L4298 ‚Äî not the normal-hit branch's `s.invuln = HIT_STUN_DURATION` at L4321, confirmed by reading both call sites in context), and `GAME_VERSION` (L242). **The problem (Paul's proposed mechanism, "try 1 second and playtest"):** the i-frame rate-limits auto-saves to ~one per `HIT_STUN_DURATION`, but during that same window the shield-off passive recharge (`+0.12/s`) was still running, netting only `‚àí0.22+0.12=‚àí0.10`/save-cycle ‚Äî ~8 saves from a full pool, a soft safety net bordering on "never dies" at critical hull. **The fix ‚Äî 1 constant + 1 field + 3 edits, exactly per the phase prompt:** `const AUTO_SHIELD_REGEN_PAUSE = 1.0;` (beside `AUTO_SHIELD_SCORE_PENALTY`, L128‚Äì131 cluster); a runtime-only `this.autoShieldRegenLock = 0;` on the ship init (no persistence, no `afd_settings_v1` change); armed via `s.autoShieldRegenLock = AUTO_SHIELD_REGEN_PAUSE;` beside `s.invuln = HIT_STUN_DURATION;` in the auto-shield branch; ticked via `if (this.autoShieldRegenLock > 0) this.autoShieldRegenLock -= dt;` right beside the `invuln` countdown; and the passive-recharge `else`-branch gated to `if (this.autoShieldRegenLock <= 0) this.energy = Math.min(1, this.energy + SHIELD_RECHARGE * dt);` ‚Äî **FLAG-3b: gated ONLY that passive branch**, the manual shield-hold `if`-branch (drain) is completely untouched, so a player can still raise the shield by hand while the lock counts down; it only withholds passive refill. Net per save-cycle is now the full `‚àí0.22` ‚Üí ~4 saves from a full pool, matching the phase's target (vs. the pre-P4 ~8). **Version bump (this phase hosts it, being the round's last):** `GAME_VERSION` `"1.0.0.12"`‚Üí`"1.0.0.13"`; grepped `scratchpad/` for the old literal and bumped the one hit (`test-cs010-p0.js`, 6 occurrences across its header comment + two assertion sections). **New test `scratchpad/test-cs013-p4.js`** (25 assertions, drives the REAL `damageShip`/`game.ship.update(dt)` directly ‚Äî no energy-math reimplementation; `keys` is returned from the harness so the manual-shield branch can be driven headlessly by setting `keys["shift"]` directly, the same technique `kbActive`/`bindings.shield` use for a real held key): source markers + `node --check`; a real auto-save arms the lock to exactly `AUTO_SHIELD_REGEN_PAUSE`; passive regen stays frozen through a mid-window tick AND a big-dt tick spanning the rest of the window (the shield block reads the PRE-decrement lock value, so even the exact transition frame stays gated), then resumes the very next frame by exactly `SHIELD_RECHARGE*dt`; the lock decrements by `dt` every frame regardless of whether the manual shield is held; holding the shield manually still drains `SHIELD_DRAIN*dt` and raises `shieldOn` normally while the lock is active (FLAG-3b); driving hits at the real i-frame cadence (a single big-dt tick of `HIT_STUN_DURATION+0.01` between each) nets exactly 4 saves before the 5th lands as real damage (was ~8 pre-P4); a `GAME_VERSION === "1.0.0.13"` pin; headless no-crash smoke. **`test-cs012-p5.js`'s energy-self-limit section (E) updated:** that section's loop never actually called `Ship.update()` (it manually jumps `s.invuln = 0` to simulate the i-frame lapsing), so it was ALREADY exercising the no-recharge floor before this phase too ‚Äî confirmed by running it unmodified against the P4 build first (still passed, 4-in-range, unchanged); tightened its assertion from a `saves >= 4 && saves <= 5` range to the now-guaranteed exact `saves === 4`, with a comment pointing future readers to the new dedicated test for the recharge-timing-sensitive assertions this section's shortcut loop structurally can't exercise. Full regression: **53 test files, 4,407 assertions**, `node --check` clean. **Prior session (CS013 P3):** implemented CS013 Phase 3 (Group B, ¬ß2.3 of `PLANNED-FEATURES-CS013.md`), reading `STATUS.md` first as required, re-grepping every anchor before editing per the phase prompt's own instruction (they'd drifted a handful of lines from the planning doc's estimates, same pattern as P1/P2) ‚Äî `drawAchievements` (planning-doc-estimated L5340, actual L5373 pre-edit), `drawAchRow` (estimated L5364, actual L5389 pre-edit), `menuAchievements` (estimated L2424, actual L2436 pre-edit), `gotoScreen` (estimated L2317, actual L2324 pre-edit). Depends on P2 (reuses `COLOR.menuIdle`), landed after it as sequenced. **The problem:** at the viewer's pre-P3 size, the size-10 `COLOR.dim` descriptions were near-illegible, and Paul asked for √ó1.5 with a scroll fallback if the bigger text overflowed the panel ‚Äî which it does (the 10 lifetime rows' last row lands at `y+670`, past both the 660-tall panel and the footer). **¬ß2.3.1 ‚Äî √ó1.5 sizing:** added `const ACH_SCALE = 1.5;` and `const ACH_SCROLL_STEP = 60;` beside `MENU_HINT_SIZE` (actual L2248-2249, the menu-tuning constant cluster, not the achievement-logic `ACH_TOAST_TIME` block near the top of the file ‚Äî these two tune viewer *rendering*, same family as `MENU_HINT_SIZE`). Every size in `drawAchievements`/`drawAchRow` now multiplies by `ACH_SCALE` at the call site (name 15, tier-status 13, single-goal progress 14, description 10, column headers 15, subtitle 12) rather than hardcoding scaled literals; `step` 40‚Üí`40*ACH_SCALE`(60); the intra-row description offset `ry+15`‚Üí`ry+22`. Fit-checked the header (`y+108`)/subtitle (`y+74`) baselines against the size bump ‚Äî comfortably clear (34px gap, only the subtitle's ~18px-tall glyphs and header's ~22.5px ones, no overlap) ‚Äî and row 0 against the header ‚Äî tight (header's descent-free caps end ~y+112, row 0's cap-height ascent starts ~y+114, a hair's width) but workable without a resize, matching the planning doc's own prediction; **no panel resize needed**. The footer is now routed through **`drawMenuHint`** (P2's helper) instead of a separate `12*ACH_SCALE` literal, per FLAG-2e ‚Äî one less duplicated footer, `MENU_HINT_SIZE`/`COLOR.menuIdle`, same position (`y+644`). **¬ß2.3.2 ‚Äî contrast:** the description (`COLOR.dim`, both the tiered and single-goal `drawAchRow` branches) and the locked/incomplete progress readout (tiered `idx<0` branch, single-goal not-done branch) now read `COLOR.menuIdle`; unlocked stays `COLOR.ach` gold, tier tints (`TIER_COLOR[idx]`) are untouched. **¬ß2.3.3 ‚Äî the scroll machinery (the only new machinery in CS013, `ultrathink`'d per the phase prompt):** `game.menu.scroll = 0` added to the `game.menu` literal (actual L3525) and reset in `gotoScreen` (actual L2326) beside the index/row/col resets ‚Äî every screen entry, not just the first, starts unscrolled. `menuAchievements` (actual L2438) gained `up`/`down` branches (previously unused by this read-only screen) adjusting `game.menu.scroll` by `ACH_SCROLL_STEP`, clamped to `[0, achMaxScroll()]` ‚Äî keyboard and gamepad d-pad/L-stick both already normalize to `"up"/"down"` through `menuInput`, so one branch covers both input methods (FLAG-2c). **The maxScroll derivation (the "one non-mechanical bit"):** a new shared `achMaxScroll()` (actual L5391, placed just above `drawAchievements` since both it and `menuAchievements` need the identical ceiling) computes `rowsTall = max(activeWeekly().length, ceil(LIFETIME.length/2))` ‚Äî driven by the ACTUAL row counts, never hardcoded, so a future pool resize keeps working ‚Äî then `contentH = (rowsTall-1)*ACH_ROW_STEP + 22 + 10*ACH_SCALE` (last row's baseline to its description's bottom) minus `ACH_ROW_VISIBLE_H` (the clipped interior height), floored at 0. Panel/row geometry (`ACH_PANEL_W/H`, `ACH_PANEL_Y`, `ACH_ROW0_Y`, `ACH_ROW_STEP`, `ACH_ROW_CLIP_TOP/BOTTOM`, `ACH_ROW_VISIBLE_H`, actual L5379-5385) was hoisted to top-level consts rather than locals inside `drawAchievements` specifically so `achMaxScroll()` ‚Äî called from `menuAchievements()`, which has no drawing context ‚Äî derives the exact same numbers the renderer clips against, without re-invoking `menuPanel()` (which has fill/stroke/text side effects and can't run twice a frame); this is safe because the panel's position is fully deterministic (fixed `VIEW_W/VIEW_H` and the panel's own fixed 1200√ó660). With the real 20-entry LIFETIME this computes to `maxScroll ‚âà 71px` (a little over one `ACH_SCROLL_STEP`). **Clip:** `ctx.save()/beginPath()/rect(x, ACH_ROW_CLIP_TOP, ACH_PANEL_W, ACH_ROW_VISIBLE_H)/clip()` wraps only the three columns' `drawAchRow` calls (each row offset by `- game.menu.scroll`), `ctx.restore()` before anything else ‚Äî the panel frame/title (drawn via `menuPanel`, unchanged, before the clip even opens), column headers, subtitle, the `‚ñ≤`/`‚ñº` cue, and the footer all draw outside the bracket and never scroll. **Affordance:** a `‚ñ≤`/`‚ñº` `COLOR.menuIdle` text cue (size 16) ‚Äî `‚ñ≤` shown only when `scroll > 0` (something scrolled past above), `‚ñº` only when `scroll < maxScroll` (something still below) ‚Äî both gated on `maxScroll > 0` overall so a short pool shows neither. **FLAG-2d (column width) ‚Äî kept the 3-column layout, did not build the 2-column fallback**, per the doc's explicit "ship the 3-column version" instruction; `colW=350` is marginal for √ó1.5 descriptions and an over-long one may clip, which is Paul's call to revisit in playtest, not something to pre-solve. **New test `scratchpad/test-cs013-p3.js`** (267 assertions, drives the REAL `drawAchievements`/`drawAchRow`/`menuAchievements`/`gotoScreen`/`achMaxScroll` via a recording-canvas stub logging `fillText` [text/x/y/font-size/color/align] AND `save`/`beginPath`/`rect`/`clip`/`restore` into one ORDERED log so bracket order is assertable ‚Äî mirrors `test-cs012-p2.js`/`test-cs013-p2.js`'s canvas-recording idiom, no menu-render logic reimplemented; a local `resetAch()` test-scaffolding helper mirrors `test-f9.js`'s own, but deliberately keeps `activeIds` at the real 5-wide weekly slice rather than f9's "activate all 16" tweak ‚Äî that tweak is right for f9's gameplay-trigger coverage but would silently inflate the weekly column's row count here and mask a real bug in `achMaxScroll`, which is exactly what caught it during authoring): (A) `node --check`; **Prior session (CS012 P5):** implemented CS012 Phase 5 ‚Äî the **auto-shield** difficulty option (`IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-012.md` P5): a reactive last-resort save at critical hull, **default OFF**. **The load-bearing part was the `damageShip` hook** ‚Äî a block at the TOP of `damageShip`, *before* the `if (s.dead || s.shieldOn || s.invuln > 0) return false;` early-return: when `settings.autoShield` is on and `!s.dead && !s.shieldOn && s.invuln <= 0 && s.hp <= LOW_HP_THRESHOLD && s.energy >= SHIELD_HIT_COST`, it spends `SHIELD_HIT_COST` energy, applies the **same knockback (copied `shortDelta`/`atan2`/`KNOCKBACK_SPEED` body) + `s.invuln = HIT_STUN_DURATION`** a real hit would, sets `s.shieldOn = true`, deducts the new `AUTO_SHIELD_SCORE_PENALTY` (500) **directly from `game.score` (clamped ‚â• 0) ‚Äî bypassing `addScore`, never touching `game.nextRepair` (FLAG-4e)** ‚Äî pushes a `COLOR.lowhp` "-500" floater, and returns `false` (0 HP dealt; same contract as the shielded early-return). **The stun i-frame is what rate-limits auto-saves to ~one per second** (same-frame follow-ups hit the raised-shield early-return; subsequent-frame hits are absorbed by the i-frame until it lapses), and since recharge (0.12/s) < cost (0.22/save) the energy pool self-exhausts after ~4‚Äì5 back-to-back saves ‚Äî a deliberately expensive safety net a healthy run never notices. **What landed:** (1) `const AUTO_SHIELD_SCORE_PENALTY = 500;` by the `SHIELD_*` constants (PLAYTEST KNOB, FLAG-4d). (2) `settings.autoShield = false` default; `saveSettings` writes it; `loadSettings` accepts it only if `typeof data.autoShield === "boolean"` (additive ‚Äî no schema bump, same rule as `captions`). (3) the `damageShip` hook. (4) `DIFFICULTY_ROWS` ‚Üí `["shot","magnet","autoshield","back"]`; `menuDifficulty` gained an `autoshield` left/right branch (`settings.autoShield = a === "right"; saveSettings();`). (5) `drawDifficulty` added the "Auto-shield: Off | On" row, grew the panel (360 ‚Üí 418), added a **per-row help line** for the focused row ("Auto-raises shield at critical hull. -500 points per blocked hit."), and shifted Back/help/hint down. **`GAME_VERSION` bumped `"1.0.0.11"` ‚Üí `"1.0.0.12"`** (last player-visible phase); `test-cs010-p0.js`'s pinned literal updated. **New test `scratchpad/test-cs012-p5.js`** (48 assertions, drives the REAL `damageShip`/`saveSettings`/`loadSettings`/`menuDifficulty`): OFF baseline = full damage; ON = 0-HP save with energy/score/stun/knockback/floater and `nextRepair` untouched + score clamp at 0; same-frame no-op + i-frame absorption; energy self-limit; above-threshold + dead-ship = no save; `afd_settings_v1` round-trip (missing/non-boolean ‚Üí false, default false); `DIFFICULTY_ROWS`/`menuDifficulty` toggle both ways + persist; headless `startGame()`/`update(1/60)` no-crash. **One pre-existing test updated** ‚Äî `test-p5.js` section I (its Difficulty navigation assumed Back at index 2; the inserted auto-shield row moved Back to index 3, so it now steps through the new row and toggles it). **Full regression green: all 49 test files**, `node --check` clean. A glottal source (custom `PeriodicWave` whose harmonic-tilt "richness" is a slider; sawtooth/square selectable) on a scheduled F0 contour (declination + stressed-vowel accents + phrase-final fall; `flat` robot and `lively` variants) feeds a PARALLEL bandpass formant bank F1‚ÄìF4 (F1 direct; F2‚ÄìF4 via a damp bus so nasal murmurs damp the highs), plus a separate frication path that BYPASSES the bank (Klatt's parallel path) and an aspiration path THROUGH it (so /h/ and VOT aspiration take vowel coloring). **The four intelligibility decisions ‚Äî what P9 must not lose in porting:** (1) formants RAMP through per-consonant LOCUS targets (pin-previous-then-ramp on each `AudioParam`; /b d g/ live in where F2 comes from, and the velar locus is vowel-dependent ‚Äî front ‚âà2300 Hz, back ‚âà1300 Hz); (2) stops are closure ‚Üí typed burst ‚Üí aspiration with DELAYED voicing onset (VOT ‚âà45 ms voiceless, ‚âà10 ms + voice bar voiced); (3) fricative noise is spectrally typed (/s/ 5.8 kHz strong, /sh/ 2.9 kHz, /f Œ∏/ weak + diffuse) on the bypass path; (4) the shipping lines never touch rule G2P ‚Äî a HAND dictionary covers every corpus word, the naive rule guesser serves only freeform typing and flags its guesses, and the derived ARPAbet string is EDITABLE per line (‚úé hand-fixes persist in-session and export). UI: every shipping line as a one-click button grouped by trigger; text input + editable phoneme box; a timeline canvas (F1/F2/F3 tracks on log-Hz, frication/burst bands, pitch trace, live playhead); 17 sliders + 3 selects across Pitch & pacing / Glottal source / Formants / Consonants / Radio; Play-all; a Dump panel emitting paste-ready `VOICE_PARAMS` + `VOICE_LINES` ‚Äî THE porting source. **RADIO CHAIN (spec fallback (a)) BUILT, DEFAULT-ON:** highpass 320 ‚Üí lowpass 3200 ‚Üí tanh soft-clip ‚Üí compressor, plus a squelch-keyed static bed; band-limiting concentrates energy where intelligibility lives (telephone-speech effect), so radio-Dan is expected to BEAT the clean synth, and the A/B is one checkbox. **CORPUS COUNT CORRECTED ‚Äî the phase prompt says "25 including the dock/full tiers" but its own enumeration totals 24** (9 health + 5 collected + 5 expired + 4 dock + 1 full), and ¬ß11f agrees: built all 24, Paul's phrasing VERBATIM (test-pinned), invented nothing. **HONEST CEILING (pre-listen, stated for the record):** early-DECtalk/Votrax territory ‚Äî an unmistakable talking machine; sibilants, stressed vowels and prosody carry it; expected weak spots are /Œ∏ √∞/ (weak by nature), /l/-vs-/r/ (the F3-dip cue is approximated), and unstressed function words; it will NOT pass for a person and was never going to. **CS010 P3 ‚Äî PLAYTEST ASK (needs eyes in a browser, not just a passing test):** (a) **The `LOWHP_GLOW_*` numbers.** Shipped first-pass: `LOWHP_GLOW_ALPHA_MIN` 0.10, `LOWHP_GLOW_ALPHA_MAX` 0.26, `LOWHP_GLOW_RADIUS` 280 px, two-stop linear gradient (opaque corner ‚Üí transparent at radius). Two of the four corners are occupied ‚Äî top-right is the HULL/CARGO rings (the HULL ring is pulsing red *in phase* with the glow), bottom-left is the powerup rows + SCOOP pips ‚Äî so the open question is whether the glow **frames** those corners or **washes out** the rings sitting ~150 px in. If it washes: drop `ALPHA_MAX`/`RADIUS`, or concentrate the falloff by adding a mid color-stop (e.g. `0.55 ‚Üí peak¬∑0.25`) so the glow is bright at the very corner and faint by mid-radius. (b) **Does the synced hull-ring + glow + siren read as ONE alarm?** That's the whole point of FORK-2(a) ‚Äî three red HP tells at one HP-ramped rate instead of two red pulses beating out of phase. If the single rate reads as *too* much red at once, the lever is to keep the siren/glow synced but let the hull ring keep a hair of independent character ‚Äî but try the fully-synced version first, it's what was asked for. (c) **`LOWHP_RELIEF_FLASH` 0.5 s** ‚Äî long enough to register as "you're okay," short enough not to linger. (d) The corner glow is FORK-3(a) a fill, shipped as signed off; there is no `LOWHP_GLOW_MODE` toggle to compare against a stroke variant (deliberately ‚Äî Paul picked). If the fill ever needs re-litigating, ¬ß3.2 and the `drawHUD` block comment record exactly why a fill beat a `glowStroke` arc.

**CS010 P2 ‚Äî towed-mass retune: decisions, tables, and the FLAG-3a stress.** All four mass coefficients are PLAYTEST KNOBS; the numbers below are a first pass, not finals. *Why lean on the tug:* thrust/top-speed are `1/(1+m¬∑k)`, which **asymptotes** ‚Äî raising `k` can't bite the mid range without over-penalising the full 24-chain (which v3.0 P6 deliberately tuned) ‚Äî so those got only a modest firming, and the **tug** (`CARGO_MASS`, `min(1.4, m¬∑k)`) carried the mid-range fix: 0.07‚Üí0.10 moves the 1.4 cap from m‚âà20 to m=14, strengthening the low-to-mid pull-back **without touching the full-24 endpoint** (capped in both).

Handling multipliers, OLD ‚Üí NEW:

| towed mass m | thrust (k 0.06‚Üí0.07) | top speed (k 0.03‚Üí0.035) | tug min(1.4,m¬∑k) (0.07‚Üí0.10) |
|---|---|---|---|
| 6  | 73.5% ‚Üí 70.4% | 84.7% ‚Üí 82.6% | 0.42 ‚Üí 0.60 |
| 12 | 58.1% ‚Üí 54.3% | 73.5% ‚Üí 70.4% | 0.84 ‚Üí 1.20 |
| 24 | 41.0% ‚Üí 37.3% | 58.1% ‚Üí 54.3% | 1.40 ‚Üí 1.40 (capped both) |

`CARGO_TURN` candidate table (step 4) ‚Äî turn-rate multiplier `1/(1+m¬∑CARGO_TURN)` a heavy chain keeps. Shipped at **0.0** (no penalty). If enabling, suggest ~0.02‚Äì0.03 (a full 24-chain still turns at ~58‚Äì68%; 0.05 is sluggish at 45%):

| CARGO_TURN | m=6 | m=12 | m=24 |
|---|---|---|---|
| 0.01 | 94.3% | 89.3% | 80.6% |
| 0.02 | 89.3% | 80.6% | 67.6% |
| 0.03 | 84.7% | 73.5% | 58.1% |
| 0.05 | 76.9% | 62.5% | 45.5% |

FLAG-3a chain-stability re-run (`test-cs010-p2.js` (D), 24 nodes / 900 frames; HEAD = pre-CS010 coeffs):

| stress | dt | HEAD | worktree | Œî | note |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| kinematic v=420/260 (documented (E) method) | 1/60 | 4.11px | 4.11px | 0.000 | envelope holds; retune neutral (kinematic isolates the solver) |
| faithful, mass 24 | 0.05 | 8.33px | 8.17px | ‚àí0.16 | retune marginally *stabilising* |
| faithful, mass 12 | 0.05 | 10.09px | 9.19px | ‚àí0.90 | " |
| faithful, mass 6 (light+fast) | 0.05 | 12.61px | 11.61px | ‚àí0.99 | " |
| kinematic v=420/260 (over-stress) | 0.05 | 14.80px | 14.80px | 0.000 | big-timestep artifact, both builds |

No NaN, no velocity blowup anywhere. **Record-correction:** the documented 4.11px is a **dt=1/60** figure (GDD ¬ß3.4's "dt ‚â§ 0.05" bounds sim validity, not the measurement dt); the deliberately-unphysical v=420 (21px/frame) at the 0.05 clamp gives ~14.8px on *both* builds. The tug's 1.4 cap is unchanged and a stronger tug is a stronger restoring force, so the retune is stability-neutral at the documented method and marginally stabilising under realistic dt=0.05 physics.

**Proposed, NOT shipped ‚Äî the missing half of "inertia" (step 4).** Towed mass still doesn't affect **stopping**: `SHIP_DRAG` is constant and `maxSp` is a thrust ceiling, not a coasting clamp ‚Äî so a heavy chain speeds up slower but stops just as fast. If turn (`CARGO_TURN`) + tug isn't enough after playtest, the honest next lever is a load-scaled coast: e.g. an effective drag of `SHIP_DRAG √ó (1 ‚àí m¬∑k_stop)` (rough `k_stop ‚âà 0.01` lets a mass-24 chain coast ~24% longer) or clamping coasting speed to `maxSp`, not only thrusting speed. Left as a proposal with sketch numbers (to be tuned in a lab), NOT shipped, per the phase's "don't silently change the thrust/maxspd formula" rule.

**Prior session (CS009 P5): bank feedback ‚Äî powerBank state, ring scale-pop, +Ns badge.** Implemented Phase 5 of the HUD rebuild per `PLANNED-FEATURES-CS009.md` ¬ß5.1 ‚Äî banking (a same-type pickup while the effect is already active) now has a visible tell, closing the "banking is invisible" gap Phase 4 flagged. **New state** `game.powerBank` and `game.powerBankAmt` (both `{ rapid, triple, magnet, engine }`, init all-0), declared beside `game.powerFx`/`game.powerBudget` (asteroids-deluxe.html:~2592) and reset in `startGame()` (~2633) alongside them. `powerBank[t]` is seconds of bank-flash remaining (0 = none, counts down from `HUD_BANK_FLASH` 0.6s ‚Äî an existing P1-reserved constant, finally used); `powerBankAmt[t]` is the "+Ns" (or "+N" in count mode) badge number. **Armed in `applyPowerup()`** (~2900-2913): the critical ordering is `powerActive(type)` is checked **before** the `+=` that banks the effect ‚Äî this is what distinguishes a bank (effect was already running when this pickup landed) from a fresh pickup (it wasn't); a fresh pickup arms neither map, matching the phase prompt's test (A). On a bank, `powerBank[type] = HUD_BANK_FLASH` and `powerBankAmt[type] = powerDuration(type)` in time mode (30 for magnet, 15 for the rest ‚Äî **called**, never a literal, since that's the exact FLAG-F regression the prompt named) or `POWERUP_BUDGET[type]` in count mode. Both the time-mode and count-mode branches got their own `if (powerActive(type))` guard since they're separate branches of the same `if/else`. **Decay in `update()`** (~3752, immediately after the existing `powerFx` decay loop): `game.powerBank[k] = Math.max(0, game.powerBank[k] - dt)` for each type ‚Äî not in `drawHUD()`, same `Capture.hudVisible` reasoning as every prior eased/timed HUD value in this rebuild (P1's `hudHull`, P3's `cargoFlash`). **Rendered in the powerup row loop** (Phase 4's ring renderer, ~4589-4606): while `powerBank[t] > 0`, `k = powerBank[t] / HUD_BANK_FLASH` (1‚Üí0) scales a second stroked ring at `HUD_FX_RING_R * (1 + HUD_BANK_POP * k)` (a 25% pop that settles back to the ring's normal radius) in the row's `color`, and draws `"+" + powerBankAmt[t] + "s"` (bare count, no "s", in count mode) in `COLOR.ach` at `globalAlpha = k` to the right of the number (x=104, same y as the seconds text) ‚Äî `globalAlpha` is restored to 1 immediately after, inside the `if (game.powerBank[t] > 0)` block, so it can never leak into the next row or the frame (same leak-guard pattern as every prior alpha-pulse in this file). **Tests:** new `scratchpad/test-cs009-p5.js` (21 assertions) drives the REAL `applyPowerup()`/`update()`/`startGame()` directly (no HUD/canvas recording needed ‚Äî this phase is pure state, the render is a straightforward read of it): (A) a first `applyPowerup("rapid")` arms no badge; (B) a second call while active arms `powerBank.rapid === HUD_BANK_FLASH` and `powerBankAmt.rapid === 15`; (C) the same for magnet gives `powerBankAmt.magnet === 30` (the FLAG-F regression check), plus a count-mode magnet case asserting the badge equals `POWERUP_BUDGET.magnet`, not a literal; (D) `powerBank.rapid` decays to exactly 0 within `HUD_BANK_FLASH` sec of simulated `update()` calls; (E) `startGame()` clears all four keys of both maps after banks were armed. **Full regression green:** all pre-existing CS009 test files (P1-P4, 79 assertions) still pass unchanged, plus the new 21. `node --check` clean on the freshly extracted script block. **GDD not yet touched** ‚Äî same standing convention as P1-P4, deferred until the visual phases (P2-P6) all land. Did NOT push (Paul's call).**

**Prior session (CS009 P4): implemented Phase 4 of the HUD rebuild per `PLANNED-FEATURES-CS009.md` ¬ß5 + FORK-3 + FORK-5 ‚Äî the active-powerup rows are now rings instead of fill bars, closing FORK-3 (banking overshoots the ring ‚Üí overcharge halo) and FORK-5 (count mode has no denominator ‚Üí track-only).** **Replaced** the active-powerup bar loop in `drawHUD()` (the old `strokeRect`/`fillRect` block, asteroids-deluxe.html:~4547) with a ring-per-row renderer. Still iterates `POWERUP_DROP_TYPES` (rapid/triple/magnet/engine, stable order) gated by `powerActive(t)` ‚Äî that order and that single predicate are load-bearing and are NOT inlined. **Rows stack UPWARD from a fixed baseline** (`y = HUD_FX_BASE_Y - i * HUD_FX_ROW_H`), so an expiring powerup can't make the rows below it jump ‚Äî the shipped code stacked *downward* off a moving `row` cursor, which did exactly that. **Row index 0 is reserved for the SCOOP pips** (Phase 6 moves them to the stable floor); the powerup rows start at `i = 1` and float above, with an inline comment saying why. A local `slot` counter (init 1, `slot++` per active row) compacts only the ACTIVE types into consecutive rows, so gaps between inactive types leave no holes (verified by a test: with only magnet active it takes slot 1, the bottom row). **Each row:** a `COLOR.dim` full-circle track **always drawn** (`ctx.arc(40, y, HUD_FX_RING_R, 0, TAU)` + stroke, no glow ‚Äî direct, not via `drawRingArc` which is arc-only) so the row's SHAPE is identical across modes; the type glyph dead center via `drawPowerupGlyph(t, 40, y, HUD_FX_GLYPH_R, color)` ‚Äî the **existing** L2411 double-chevron/fan/horseshoe/bell set that already matches the field pickup (the brief's chevron/diamond icons are superseded, no new icons authored); and `POWERUP_LABEL[t]` at x=64 size 13 with the number beneath it at x=64 size 16. **TRAP 1 (denominator differs by type) ‚Äî handled:** time-mode fill is `game.powerFx[t] / powerDuration(t)`, and `powerDuration()` returns 30 for magnet / 15 for the rest ‚Äî the function is called, never `POWERUP_DURATION` directly (miss it and the magnet ring renders permanently over-full; P4 test ¬ßA asserts a `powerFx.magnet = 30` ring sweeps exactly ONE turn, not two). **TRAP 2 / FORK-3 A (banking overshoots) ‚Äî the overcharge halo:** `applyPowerup` banks (`powerFx += powerDuration`), so a double-banked Rapid is 30s / 15s = frac 2.0. The main arc draws `clamp01(frac)` (pinned at a full turn); when `frac > 1`, a **second, thinner arc at radius `HUD_FX_RING_R + 4`** draws `clamp01(frac - 1)` ‚Äî a full ring with a halo, so the surplus stays legible instead of pinning at 100% for 15 straight seconds (which reads as broken). Not just clamped-and-dropped. **TRAP 3 / FORK-5 (count mode has no denominator) ‚Äî track only:** `powerMode(t)` returns `"time"`/`"shots"`/`"pieces"` from player settings (`settings.shotPowerupMode`, `settings.magnetMode` ‚Äî the two shipped Difficulty options); in count mode the budget banks with no ceiling, so the row draws the dim track + glyph + `String(game.powerBudget[t])` where the seconds would go, and **no value arc** (kept the shipped `const counted = powerMode(t) !== "time"` branch; P4 test ¬ßC asserts zero value arc for a `magnetMode = "pieces"` row). **Seconds text is `Math.ceil(game.powerFx[t]) + "s"`** ‚Äî ceil not round, so a ring reading "1s" hasn't already expired. **Low-timer warning:** `game.powerFx[t] <= HUD_FX_LOW` (3s) ‚Üí ring, glyph, label, and seconds all shift to `COLOR.lowhp` and pulse at `HUD_PULSE_HZ`, reusing Phase 2's exact `globalAlpha` sine idiom (restored to 1 immediately after each row so it can't leak into the next row or the frame). **Time mode ONLY** ‚Äî a budget of 2 shots is not a deadline (FLAG-E), so count mode never state-colors (P4 test ¬ßE asserts a 2-shot count budget stays un-warned). **Scope discipline:** the CARGO-block `row += 26` line is kept (its comment updated) because the SCOOP-pip block below still reads `row` ‚Äî SCOOP relocation to the bottom-left floor (spec ¬ß6) is Phase 6, not this phase; SCOOP pips stay where P3 left them. **Tests:** new `scratchpad/test-cs009-p4.js` (21 assertions) drives REAL `startGame()`/`drawHUD()` against a recording ctx that reconstructs each arc stroke (center/radius/sweep/color/width) ‚Äî the four required checks (A: magnet full-turn not two; B: double-banked ‚Üí main arc full + halo at +4, plus a partial-bank 1.5‚Üíhalf-turn halo and a frac<1 ‚Üí no-halo case; C: count mode ‚Üí track only, no value arc; D: zero `fillRect` + zero `strokeRect` in the whole `drawHUD()`) plus low-timer time-vs-count coloring (E) and fixed-baseline compaction (F). **Three pre-existing `test-p5.js` assertions flipped** (same supersession pattern as P2): K2 (was: magnet bar fill width proves denominator 30) now asserts the fill bar is GONE and points at P4 test ¬ßA for the denominator invariant; L4/L5 (was: count-mode plain number at x=58 / time-mode bar) now assert the number moved to x=64, no fill bar in either mode, and time mode draws `Ns` seconds text ‚Äî `test-p5.js` 80‚Üí84 assertions. **Full regression green: all 28 test files, 1861 assertions** (1840 P3 baseline + 21 new P4). `node --check` clean on the freshly extracted script block. **GDD not yet touched** ‚Äî same standing convention as P1/P2/P3, deferred until the visual phases (P2-P6) all land. Did NOT push (Paul's call).**

**Prior session (CS009 P3): implemented Phase 3 of the HUD rebuild per `PLANNED-FEATURES-CS009.md` ¬ß4 + FORK-2 ‚Äî the CARGO ring, matching the P2 HULL ring's geometry and animation idiom, and closing FORK-2's runtime-denominator + cap-up-flash design.** Deleted the left-column `drawText("CARGO " + game.chain.length + "/" + game.cargoMax, ...)` line (asteroids-deluxe.html:~4503) and replaced it with a ring at `(HUD_CARGO_CX 1232, HUD_RING_CY 74)`, same construction as HULL's: a full-circle dim track (`COLOR.dim`, `HUD_RING_TRACK_W`, no glow, drawn direct ‚Äî not through `drawRingArc`) then a value arc via `drawRingArc(HUD_CARGO_CX, HUD_RING_CY, HUD_RING_R, clamp01(game.chain.length / game.cargoMax), cargoColor, cargoRingW)`. **`game.cargoMax` is read live every frame, never cached or literal-substituted** ‚Äî it's the runtime value that grows `CARGO_BASE` 12 ‚Üí `CARGO_CAP_MAX` 24, +1 per `CARGO_GROW_PER` 30 canisters delivered (L3762-3766), so caching it would freeze the ring's meaning stale the moment a cap-up landed. **Center content** is `String(game.chain.length)` at size 20 (`COLOR.text` when the chain is non-empty, `COLOR.dim` when empty ‚Äî preserves the shipped ternary tell verbatim) with `"/" + game.cargoMax` beneath it at size 11 in `COLOR.dim`, and a centered `drawText("CARGO", HUD_CARGO_CX, HUD_RING_LABEL_Y, 13, COLOR.dim, "center")` label ‚Äî note the center TEXT color is never gilded, only the ring arc is (FORK-2 A's spec draws that line precisely: the number stays legible at every state). **Full-cap and cap-up-flash share one gold idiom, matching the HULL ring's MAX state exactly** ‚Äî `cargoGold = cargoFull || game.cargoFlash > 0` drives both the arc color (`COLOR.ach`) and a `HUD_PULSE_HZ` pulse (`globalAlpha` sine, always restored to 1 immediately after, same leak-guard as P2). Gold now means exactly one thing everywhere in the HUD: "this resource is at its cap; more is wasted." **New `game.cargoFlash` state** (init `0`, reset in `startGame()`) is armed to `HUD_CAP_FLASH` (0.5s, a P1-reserved constant put to use here) at the cap-grow site (asteroids-deluxe.html:~3763, the `if (growCap > game.cargoMax)` block) alongside the existing `"TOW +1"` ship-position `FloatText` ‚Äî a **second, separate** `FloatText("+1 CAP", game.dock.x, game.dock.y - 22, COLOR.ach)` is pushed **at the dock**, not the ship, per spec: "the reward should read where it was earned." While armed, the ring also **thickens** to `HUD_RING_W + 2` (`cargoRingW`), on top of the gold + pulse, so a cap-up is legible even mid-scroll. **Decay is linear** (`game.cargoFlash = Math.max(0, game.cargoFlash - dt)`), placed in `update()` immediately after the existing `hudHull` ease line (asteroids-deluxe.html:~3630-3633) ‚Äî same Capture.hudVisible reasoning as P1: a decay gated on drawHUD() would freeze while `H` hides the HUD and pop back stale on re-show. **Rationale documented inline at both the constant and the arm site**: a cap-up mechanically *shrinks* the ring's fraction (the same chain is now a smaller slice of a bigger cap) ‚Äî without the flash that reads as a bug, not a promotion (FORK-2 A's own framing, quoted in-code). **Left-column layout preserved**: removing the CARGO text line would have shifted the powerup rows up 26px as an incidental side effect outside this phase's scope, so the `row += 26` increment that used to follow the CARGO text is kept (now a standalone line with a comment explaining why), leaving every row below it exactly where P1/P2 left it. **Tests:** new `scratchpad/test-cs009-p3.js` (12 assertions) drives REAL dock deliveries (same `fillChain`/`tickDock` idiom as the F9 achievement test's C2 block ‚Äî park the dock on the ship, push chain nodes directly, call the real `update()` with `dt > DOCK_OFFLOAD_INTERVAL` so exactly one canister peels off per call) through a real `CARGO_GROW_PER`-canister cap-up: (A) `cargoFlash` arms to exactly `HUD_CAP_FLASH` on the single `update()` call where `cargoMax` actually increments ‚Äî not before, not one call later (caught a real off-by-one: an extra `update()` call after the arming frame decays it, so the test drives exactly one call for that assertion); (B) it decays to 0 within `HUD_CAP_FLASH` sec of simulated real time; (C) `startGame()` clears both `cargoFlash` and `cargoMax`; (D) `cargoMax` still stops climbing at `CARGO_CAP_MAX` even after several multiples of `CARGO_GROW_PER` more deliveries than needed. **Full regression green: all 27 test files, 1840 assertions** (1828 P2 baseline + 12 new). `node --check` clean on the freshly extracted script block. **GDD not yet touched** ‚Äî same standing convention as P1/P2, deferred until the visual phases (P2-P6) all land. **Prior session (CS009 P2): implemented Phase 2 of the HUD rebuild per `PLANNED-FEATURES-CS009.md` ¬ß3 + FORK-1 ‚Äî the flagship HULL ring is now live, replacing BOTH the hull HP fill bar and the shield energy fill bar (the first real visual change of the CS009 rebuild).** In `drawHUD()` (asteroids-deluxe.html:~4460) the two left-column fill-bar blocks ‚Äî hull (`strokeRect`/`fillRect` + gold `MAX` text tag) and shield (`strokeRect`/`fillRect` + `SHIELD` label) ‚Äî are **deleted** and replaced by a single top-right "ship status" element at `(HUD_HULL_CX 1156, HUD_RING_CY 74)`: (1) a **full-circle dim track** (`COLOR.dim`, `HUD_RING_TRACK_W` 2, no glow ‚Äî drawn direct with `ctx.arc(...,0,TAU)`+`stroke`, not via `drawRingArc` which is arc-only); (2) a **concentric shield arc** at `HUD_RING_R - HUD_SHIELD_R_GAP` (r21), fraction `game.ship.energy` (un-eased ‚Äî energy is already continuous), `COLOR.shield` `#40b0ff`, thinner (`HUD_RING_TRACK_W + 1` = 3), **never state-colored** (it's a separate resource); (5) a centered `drawText("HULL", HUD_HULL_CX, HUD_RING_LABEL_Y, 13, COLOR.dim, "center")` label. **Three mutually-exclusive states, precedence MAX > Critical > Normal, tested against the TRUE `game.ship.hp` (never the eased `hudHull`) so the color flips the instant the hit lands even though the arc lags ~0.35s**: MAX (`hp >= SHIP_MAX_HP` ‚Üí `COLOR.ach` gold, no pulse ‚Äî the gold ring **replaces** the retired `MAX` text tag and carries the same v3.6 FLAG-E meaning "a Health pickup would be wasted"); Critical (`hp <= LOW_HP_THRESHOLD` 100 = 40% ‚Äî the **shared** siren/low-HP-chevron threshold, not a new HUD-only one ‚Üí `COLOR.lowhp` `#ff4040`, **pulsing**); Normal (else ‚Üí `COLOR.hp` `#5fe08a`). **The pulse** (`ctx.globalAlpha = 0.6 + 0.4*Math.sin(performance.now()/1000 * TAU * HUD_PULSE_HZ)`, constant `HUD_PULSE_HZ` 1.2 ‚Äî deliberately NOT ramped with HP urgency, since `lowhpSet()` already ramps the audio siren and two nearby ramps read as a wobble, spec FLAG-D) wraps ONLY the hull arc + glyph (the shield arc is drawn first, at full alpha) and `globalAlpha` is **always restored to 1** immediately after (a leak would tint the rest of the frame). `clamp01` is applied at the `drawRingArc` **call site** (the helper itself never clamps ‚Äî banking/overcharge is a later phase). **Scope discipline:** this phase touches ONLY the hull/shield element. The CARGO text readout and the powerup-row `fillRect`/`strokeRect` bars are still present and unchanged ‚Äî they belong to P3 (CARGO ring) and P4/P6 (powerup rows + the final no-fills sweep). So the Phase-2 prompt's aspirational "no `fillRect`/`strokeRect` may survive in this function" is true for the two deleted blocks but NOT yet for the whole function; the powerup-row rects survive by design until P4/P6. **Tests:** new `scratchpad/test-cs009-p2.js` (33 assertions) drives the REAL `startGame()`/`drawHUD()` against a recording ctx that reconstructs each stroke's arc/poly + style state ‚Äî verifies the track/shield/hull arcs (radius, sweep, color, width), the nose-up glyph at the ring center, the `HULL` label, that the arc sweep reads eased `hudHull` while the color reads true `hp` (risk b/c), all three state colors, that the shield arc stays `COLOR.shield` + un-eased even when the hull is critical, that the pulse fires only in Critical, and that `globalAlpha` returns to 1. **Two pre-existing tests updated** for the deletion, both were green on baseline and are green again: `test-p5.js` L2/L3 (v3.6 P4) ‚Äî the SHIELD-bar-in-left-column and hull-bar-gold-at-max/MAX-tag assertions now assert those fill bars + the `MAX` text tag are **gone** (superseded by the ring); `test-v34-p5.js` `findLowhpChevron()` ‚Äî its "any `COLOR.lowhp` poly = the chevron" heuristic now also filters on vertex count (`lineTos === 2`, the 3-point chevron) so the new 4-point ship glyph (also `COLOR.lowhp` when critical) isn't miscounted as a second chevron. **Full regression green: all 26 test files, 1828 assertions** (1798 P1 baseline + 33 new ‚àí 3 net from the p5 rewrite). `node --check` clean on the freshly extracted script block. **GDD not yet touched** ‚Äî ¬ß2 will get the HUD-section rewrite once the visual phases (P2-P6) all land, per the standing per-phase convention; a single element replacing two bars mid-rebuild is noted here, not folded into ¬ß2 yet. **Prior session (CS009 P1): implemented Phase 1 of the HUD rebuild per `PLANNED-FEATURES-CS009.md` ¬ß2/¬ß3/¬ß7 ‚Äî pure plumbing, zero visual change.** The existing `drawHUD()` bars are byte-for-byte untouched; this phase only lays groundwork the later visual phases will consume. **Added a `HUD_*` constants group** (right after the v3.6 P6 `GAME_VERSION` block, before "Radioactive salvage" ‚Äî asteroids-deluxe.html:~204), one named constant per ¬ß2/¬ß3/¬ß5 value: `HUD_RING_R` 30, `HUD_RING_W` 4, `HUD_RING_TRACK_W` 2, `HUD_RING_BLUR` 12, `HUD_HULL_CX` 1156, `HUD_CARGO_CX` 1232, `HUD_RING_CY` 74, `HUD_RING_LABEL_Y` 122, `HUD_SHIELD_R_GAP` 9, `HUD_FX_BASE_Y` 640, `HUD_FX_ROW_H` 40, `HUD_FX_RING_R` 16, `HUD_FX_GLYPH_R` 9, `HUD_FX_LOW` 3, `HUD_PULSE_HZ` 1.2, `HUD_EASE` 0.002, `HUD_BANK_FLASH` 0.6, `HUD_BANK_POP` 0.25, `HUD_CAP_FLASH` 0.5 ‚Äî with a header comment marking the whole group as look-call knobs tuned in the browser, per this repo's "tuning constants at the top, never inline magic numbers" rule. **Added `drawRingArc(x, y, r, frac, color, width, blur)`** immediately after `drawPoly` (next to `glowStroke`), exactly per spec ¬ß7: arc from `-Math.PI/2`, clockwise, sweeping `TAU * frac`, routed through `glowStroke()` (never touches `ctx.strokeStyle`/`shadowBlur` directly), never `closePath()`s (an arc, not a poly), and **does not clamp `frac`** ‚Äî an explicit `if (frac <= 0) return;` early-out is the only guard; overshoot (banking, FORK-3) is the caller's job, confirmed by grep that no `Math.min`/`Math.max`/`clamp01` appears in its body. **Added `game.hudHull`** (init `1`) beside `game.powerFx`/`game.powerBudget` in the `game` object, reset to `game.ship.hp / SHIP_MAX_HP` in `startGame()` (placed after `game.ship = new Ship()`, since a fresh ship's actual HP is what it must match ‚Äî no drain animation on a new run), and advanced in **`update()`** ‚Äî inserted right after `game.ship.update(dt)`, well before the early-return for `!game.paused`/non-`playing` states ‚Äî with the dt-correct exponential smoothing from spec ¬ß3: `game.hudHull += (target - game.hudHull) * (1 - Math.pow(HUD_EASE, dt))`. **Deliberately placed the ease in `update()`, not `drawHUD()`, with a comment saying why**: `drawHUD()` is gated by `Capture.hudVisible`, so an ease running only while drawn would freeze while the HUD is hidden with `H` and then snap on re-show ‚Äî exactly the risk the phase prompt flagged. **`HUD_EASE`'s comment explicitly documents the counter-intuitive direction** (a *larger* constant means *less* damping / a *faster* chase ‚Äî same `Math.pow(CONST, dt)` idiom as the shipped `MAGNET_DAMP`, cross-referenced by line), per the phase prompt's risk (c) ‚Äî nobody should "fix" this later. **New headless test `scratchpad/test-cs009-p1.js`** (GDD ¬ß5.4 rule 7 idiom ‚Äî stub window/document/localStorage, eval the real `<script>` block, drive the real `startGame()`/`update()`/`drawRingArc()`, no reimplementation): (A) `game.hudHull` closes at least 95% of a sudden 0.8-magnitude gap (full HP ‚Üí 50/250) within 0.5s of simulated frames, matching `HUD_EASE`'s own "~0.35s to close 95%" comment; (B) frame-rate independence ‚Äî 30√ó`update(1/60)`-as-two-half-steps lands within 1% of 30√ó`update(1/30)` from the same eased start value and pinned target; (C) `startGame()` resets `hudHull` to `1` (fresh `Ship()` is full HP); (D) `drawRingArc` doesn't throw against the stubbed no-op ctx for a normal fill, an overcharge fill (`frac=1.4`, confirmed passed through unclamped), and non-positive `frac` (early-return, no throw). **Full regression re-run green: all 25 test files (24 pre-existing + the new one), 1798 assertions** (up from 1793 + the new 5). `node --check` clean on the freshly extracted script block. **No visual change shipped** ‚Äî `drawHUD()` itself is untouched in this phase; the new constants/helper/state exist but nothing in the draw path calls `drawRingArc` or reads `game.hudHull` yet (that's Phase 2+). **GDD not yet touched this phase** ‚Äî ¬ß2/¬ß3 describe the shipped HUD, which hasn't visually changed; the Architecture Map gets its update once the visual phases land, per the standing per-phase convention (a plumbing-only phase with no player-facing delta doesn't warrant a GDD edit yet). **Prior session summary (v3.6 P3): the powerup drop economy replaced: a 16%-per-small-tier-kill roll (which only ever fired from Debris/Hunter smalls ‚Äî saucers dropped nothing) is gone, replaced by three deterministic sources.** Implemented `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.6.md` Phase 2 exactly as specced, reading `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.6.md` ¬ß7/¬ß8 first and grepping the live build to confirm every line reference before editing. Two independent parts, two commits. **PART A (P2a) ‚Äî the Magnet buff.** Grep confirmed the culprit named in ¬ß7: not `MAGNET_PULL` (520, untouched) but `MAGNET_DAMP`, which at 0.06 stripped ~4.6% of a piece's velocity every frame (`Math.pow(0.06, dt)`), turning the pull into a terminal-velocity governor rather than an acceleration ‚Äî `v_terminal ‚âà accel/2.7`. Combined with the hardcoded quadratic falloff, a piece 190px out only felt ~175 px/s¬≤ and topped out near 65 px/s (~3s to arrive); the mid-field was dead. Three constants, all flagged PLAYTEST KNOBS: the falloff exponent is hoisted out of the inline `t*t` into `MAGNET_FALLOFF_POW`, shipped at `1.0` (linear ‚Äî the near field was never the problem); `MAGNET_PULL_MIN` 60‚Üí150 (governs the far field by construction); `MAGNET_DAMP` 0.06‚Üí0.35 (counter-intuitively *less* damping ‚Äî the biggest single lever, and the one flagged as riskiest for overshoot/orbiting). A code comment above the pull block in `asteroids-deluxe.html` now derives `v_terminal ‚âà accel¬∑dt / (1 - MAGNET_DAMP^dt)` so the next tuning pass reaches for `MAGNET_DAMP`, not `MAGNET_PULL`, if it still feels weak. `MAGNET_RANGE` (380) and the `accel /= ‚àömass` line are untouched, per spec. **PART B (P2b) ‚Äî large-Hunter last-stand pursuit.** `HunterSatellite.update()`'s `size===3` core still tumbles unconditionally (`this.angle += this.spinRate*dt`, unchanged), but once `game.debris.length === 0 && !game.ship.dead` it now also steers its heading toward the ship via the same wrap-aware `angleTo` + shortest-angular-delta clamp the homing branch already uses, at a new `HUNTER_LAST_STAND_TURN` (0.5 rad/s) and rebuilds `vx`/`vy` at a new `HUNTER_LAST_STAND_SPEED` (50 px/s ‚Äî deliberately slower than a medium homer at *any* wave, so it reads as a search-ender, not a second homing tier). **`this.homing` is never flipped** ‚Äî evaluated inline each frame instead, so `this.shape`/`this.inner` (baked off `homing` at construction) and the tumbling silhouette are untouched; the pursuit itself is the only tell (FLAG-G, per spec ‚Äî no silhouette change). Both new constants are commented as under-specified playtest knobs. **Tests:** extended the real two owning suites, no reimplementation. `scratchpad/test-v31-coalesce.js` gained tests (32)‚Äì(35): constants sane and `MAGNET_RANGE`/`MAGNET_PULL` untouched; the new pull is monotonically stronger than a frozen "old build" formula (computed inline as the comparison baseline) at every in-range distance; a mass-1 single at 190px measurably beats the old build's arrival time via real `update()` (1.17s vs. 2.22s ‚Äî time compared, not the constant); a piece at 400px still feels nothing. Tests (26)‚Äì(29), which hardcoded the old quadratic/`PULL_MIN`, were updated in place to read the now-parametrized `MAGNET_FALLOFF_POW`/`MAGNET_PULL_MIN` rather than duplicating stale constants ‚Äî all pre-existing assertions still pass. `scratchpad/test-f5.js` gained section (H): a core with Debris still on the field keeps its exact spawn-time velocity across 60 frames (regression guard, byte-identical `vx`/`vy`); with `game.debris` emptied, the same core's heading converges toward a wrap-aware target across a world-wrap seam (ship and core placed ~1400px apart straddling the seam so the naive angle is ~180¬∞ wrong, and far enough apart that the pursuit's turn radius ‚Äî `speed/turn` ‚âà 100px ‚Äî doesn't force it to orbit a too-close target); `shape`/`inner`/`homing` are confirmed unchanged (same references) after 120 frames of pursuit; a medium/small homer's trajectory is confirmed byte-identical whether `game.debris` is empty or not. If difficulty-gated layering is ever wanted back, the only work is re-adding `tier` fields to the `music-lab` track data and re-porting. ‚öÝÔ∏è **Prior session: v3.5 Phase 3 ‚Äî the low-health warning is a pulsed, HP-scaled alarm.** Not a `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.5.md` phase ‚Äî a standalone bugfix/polish session, confirmed against the live build by grep first, per the prompt. **The problem:** `AudioSys.lowhp(on)` was a 220 Hz sine, FM-warbled ¬±18 Hz by a 0.6 Hz LFO, at a **constant** gain of 0.05. Peers on the same sfx bus: explosion 0.5, hit 0.16, fire 0.12, thrust 0.10 (continuous), saucer 0.055 (continuous) ‚Äî it was the quietest voice in the game, a pure sine with no harmonics to cut through anything, and constant-amplitude, which the ear adapts away the longer it plays (so it got *less* audible over a long low-HP stretch). Simply raising the gain would have made it more annoying and no more noticeable ‚Äî the fix had to change the voice's SHAPE, not just its volume. **The rebuild** keeps the exact persistent-voice idiom of `thrust(on)`/`saucer(on)` (stored nodes built on `true`, torn down on `false`) but rebuilds what the voice IS: a root sine oscillator (`LOWHP_ROOT_FREQ`, unchanged 220 Hz) plus a soft harmonic partner a fifth above (`LOWHP_HARMONIC_RATIO` 1.5, at `LOWHP_HARMONIC_GAIN_FRAC` 0.35 of the root's level ‚Äî a body, so it reads as an instrument panel, not a test tone, and survives an explosion), both summed into a shared **amplitude-LFO "pulse" gain node** ‚Äî a slow cockpit-warning BEEP (not a drone): the onsets get noticed, the gaps in between keep it bearable over a long stretch. Base gain raised into `thrust`'s neighborhood (`LOWHP_GAIN_MIN` 0.08 ‚Üí `LOWHP_GAIN_MAX` 0.13) ‚Äî modest, since the pulsing does most of the perceptual work. **HP-SCALED URGENCY (FORK-3, resolved HP-scaled, not a flat beep):** a new `AudioSys.lowhpSet(t)` ‚Äî a no-op if the voice isn't live or `ctx` is null ‚Äî sets the pulse LFO's rate (`LOWHP_PULSE_RATE_MIN` 0.9 Hz ‚Üí `LOWHP_PULSE_RATE_MAX` 2.4 Hz) and the root/harmonic gain from urgency `t = 1 ‚àí hp/LOW_HP_THRESHOLD` (0 at the threshold, ~1 near death) ‚Äî gentle at 100 HP, a real alarm at 20. Called **every frame** (not edge-detected, unlike `lowhp(true)`/`(false)` themselves) from the ONE existing edge-detect site in `update()`, right after camera-follow, alongside the pre-existing siren calls ‚Äî that site only runs while playing-and-unpaused, and `killShip`/`quitToTitle`/`openPause`/`startGame` already tear the voice down, so **no new teardown site or game state was needed**. Params move via `linearRampToValueAtTime` over a new `LOWHP_PARAM_RAMP` (0.15 s, same idiom as `MusicSys.setDuck`/`setIntensity`'s cancel/setValueAtTime/ramp triplet) ‚Äî never a bare per-frame `.value` set, which zippers ‚Äî and `lowhpSet` is idempotent on `t` (a steady-HP frame reschedules nothing). All new numbers (root freq unchanged, harmonic ratio/gain, pulse rate min/max, pulse depth, gain min/max, param ramp) are named playtest knobs in the constants block, commented as such ‚Äî not agonized over, per the prompt. **Out of scope, both logged as flags, not built (per the prompt):** `POWERUP_HEALTH_GAP`/a force-spawned Health powerup on entering low-HP (FLAG-8a from v3.4 P5 ‚Äî still open, and now sharper: the urgency scaling keeps the voice gentle in the upper band, but a player can still be alarmed with nothing to point at for up to 26 s), and a synced red vignette pulse (FLAG-3b, still just a logged idea ‚Äî no visual touched). `LOW_HP_THRESHOLD` (100) untouched. **TESTS ‚Äî extended `scratchpad/test-v34-p5.js` in place** (the file that owns the low-health warning, per instruction ‚Äî no new file), driving the REAL `update()`/`damageShip()`/`applyPowerup()`/`killShip()`/`quitToTitle()`/`openPause()` ‚Äî no reimplementation: new sections **(H)-(J), 33‚Üí74 assertions (+41)**. (H) the rebuilt voice builds its pulse LFO + harmonic partner (root/harm/lfo oscillators, rootLevel/harmLevel/pulseGain/lfoGain gains) without throwing, and `lowhp(false)` nulls every stored handle (`lowhpOsc`/`lowhpGain`/`lowhpT`). (I) `lowhpSet` ‚Äî urgency at `hp = LOW_HP_THRESHOLD` is ~0 and at `hp = 1` is ~1 (driven through the real `update()` edge-detect formula, not a direct call); pulse rate and gain are monotonically non-decreasing as HP falls (swept t = 0/0.25/0.5/0.75/1, each checked against the exact linear-interpolation formula); every move is a `linearRampToValueAtTime` call, never a bare `.value` set (checked against the automation record, scoped to calls *after* construction ‚Äî construction's one-time bare `.value` set is legitimate, same carve-out as the P7 tier-1 gate test); idempotent on repeated `t` (no new ramp scheduled); a safe no-op with no live voice and with `ctx === null`. (J) ‚Äî **the load-bearing idempotency proof** ‚Äî a real 120-frame `update()` run at fixed low HP proves the per-frame `lowhpSet` call never rebuilds the node graph, verified via **object-identity snapshots** of the oscillator/gain node references (not a global oscillator-creation counter): an earlier attempt at a global `ctx.createOscillator` spy flaked at "4 extra oscillators" because `isolate()`'s helper (used throughout this file to zero `game.debris`/`game.hunters` for a clean ship-only scenario) also zeroes both wave-clear conditions, so the very next `update()` legitimately triggers a real `nextWave()` + the heartbeat system (`AudioSys.beat()`) independent of the siren ‚Äî a global counter was contaminated by those unrelated subsystems; the identity-snapshot rewrite sidesteps this entirely and is a strictly stronger proof of the actual claim ("the siren's own nodes didn't get torn down and rebuilt"). Also ported test-v34-p6's **concrete recording Web Audio stub** (mutable `currentTime`, real automation-call recording: `linearRamps`/`setValues`/`cancels`/`bareSets` per param) into this file, replacing the old Proxy-based stub that couldn't inspect gain/frequency AudioParam calls ‚Äî needed for (I)'s ramp-vs-bare-set assertions. **Full regression re-run green: all 24 test files, 1507 assertions** (up from 1466 ‚Äî only `test-v34-p5.js` changed, 33‚Üí74; no other file touched). `node --check` clean on the extracted script. Re-ran `test-p5` and `test-boundary` in isolation 15√ó each post-change (0/15 failures either) to confirm the documented pre-existing RNG flakes (¬ßG / ¬ßE respectively) didn't get worse ‚Äî this phase adds no `rand()` calls to any path either test exercises. The two logged, deliberately-untouched flags (FLAG-8a's up-to-26s pointerless window, now sharper; FLAG-3b's red vignette pulse) are candidates for a future playtest-driven session. ‚öÝÔ∏è **Prior session: v3.5 Phase 2 ‚Äî a garbage clump renders as a larger canister, not an asteroid.** This was the `IMPLEMENTATION-PHASES-v3.5.md` Phase 2 prompt. **The problem:** `Garbage.draw()`'s `pieces > 1` branch drew a 7‚Äì9 vertex jittered hull polygon (`makeClumpHull`, v3.3 P1) whose explicit design rationale was "reads as a target, not a pile of pickups" ‚Äî written while a clump was **un-hookable** (v3.2 P1's rule then in force). v3.3 P4 (9c) reversed that premise, making a clump directly **scoopable**, but the render never caught up ‚Äî players kept reading the hazard-shaped hull as something to avoid, exactly backwards from the intended "fly into it" pickup. **The fix:** `drawCanister(x, y, angle, alpha, color, scale = 1)` gained a trailing `scale` param scaling both the body poly and the hazard stripe; the two pre-existing call sites (the `pieces === 1` single and the chain-node render loop) omit the arg and are byte-identical to before ‚Äî the load-bearing regression guard. `Garbage.draw()`'s `pieces > 1` branch now draws exactly one `drawCanister` at `scale = this.radius / 7` (`= ‚àöpieces`, since `radius = 7¬∑‚àöpieces`) ‚Äî no new constant ‚Äî so the drawn long half-axis exactly equals the collision radius by construction. The `lerpColor(COLOR.garbage ‚Üí COLOR.clumpHot)` danger tint (scaled by `pieces/HUNTER_COALESCE_COUNT`) is kept as the only tell a clump is nearing the Hunter transform; the radioactive alpha flicker comes free from `drawCanister`. `this.hull` and `makeClumpHull` are **deleted entirely**, not just stopped-reading ‚Äî all three sites that held/regenerated the field (the `Garbage` constructor, the merge in `coalesceGarbage`, and the partial-scoop leftover re-derivation in the pickup pass) simply drop it. Did NOT push. **Previous session: v3.5 Phase 1 ‚Äî fix the Options music-track switch (menu repeat guard + audible Ambient).** Not a `PLANNED-FEATURES-v3.5.md` phase ‚Äî a two-part bugfix session, confirmed against the live build by grep first, part A and part B each their own commit's worth of work. **PART A ‚Äî the keyboard menu handler had no `e.repeat` guard.** Grepped the `window.addEventListener("keydown", ‚Ä¶)` handler (~L1075): its menu-open branch (`if (menuActive())`) called `handleMenuKey(k)` unconditionally, so browser key auto-repeat (~30/s while held) fired dozens of menu actions per held press. The gamepad path (`handleGamepadMenu()` ‚Üí `menuNavEdges()`) was already strictly edge-detected ‚Äî keyboard wasn't, and that asymmetry was the actual bug. On the 3-value Music Track row, a brief hold could spin the selection back to where it started ("nothing changed" from the player's view) while re-entering `MusicSys.setState()` nearly every frame ‚Äî each call discarding/rebuilding `trackGain` and restarting its 0.6 s crossfade ramp from `0.0001`, which is what pinned the music near-silent for as long as the key was held. **Fix:** one line ‚Äî the menu-open branch now returns early on `e.repeat` (still calling `preventDefault()` so the key doesn't scroll the page); the rebind-capture branch and the normal-play branch are untouched, exactly as scoped (gameplay legitimately wants held-key behavior, read from `keys{}` continuously, not via this edge). **Flagged, not silently absorbed:** the three volume sliders and the two Difficulty toggles are driven by the same branch, so a held key no longer scrubs them either ‚Äî a full 1.0‚Üí0.0 volume sweep is now 10 taps, matching gamepad feel. No throttled-repeat softening was added (deliberately out of scope ‚Äî a possible playtest follow-up if the 10-tap sweep reads as worse, not a bug to pre-emptively fix). **PART B ‚Äî `ambient`'s tier-1 foundation was inaudible, not just calm.** `buildAmbientTrack()`'s always-on tier-1 (foundation) layer carried exactly **one note per 8 s loop** (sine, gain 0.06, lowpass 300 Hz). Since tiers 2-4 don't unlock until wave 3+ (`MUSIC_LAYER_THRESHOLD`), tier-1 is the *entire* audible track at wave 1, and measured against the real scheduler over a 10 s window it produced **9** scheduled notes vs. retro's **127** and tense's **138** ‚Äî roughly 25√ó thinner, which is what actually made selecting Ambient sound like the music had stopped, not a deliberately mellow track. **Fix ‚Äî layer-data only, everything else in the music system untouched** (the scheduler, `setState`/`setIntensity`, `MUSIC_TRACKS`, `musicStateFor`, `MUSIC_LAYER_THRESHOLD`, and the title/tense/retro tracks were not read past a confirmatory grep): the foundation layer is now **two overlapping root/fifth (E2/B2) pad swells** offset every 2 s across the 8 s loop, each one's release overlapping the next one's attack, so the layer is continuously present with no silent gap anywhere in the loop; gain went 0.06‚Üí**0.075**, in family with retro's/tense's 0.075/0.08 bass. The other three tiers (pulse/harmony/lead) were nudged up the same way (0.035/0.04/0.03 ‚Üí 0.045/0.05/0.045) so the whole track reads as calm rather than muted once its higher tiers unlock. Key (E dorian), tempo (8 s loop, `stepDur` 0.5), character (slow, sparse, "long haul in the dark"), and the 4-tier gate structure are all unchanged ‚Äî Ambient is now the **calmest** track, not the **quietest**. **TESTS ‚Äî extended `scratchpad/test-v34-p6.js` in place** (the file that owns the music system, per instruction ‚Äî no new file), new sections **O (Part A) and P (Part B), +12 assertions (140‚Üí152)**, driving the REAL `keydown` listener(s)/`MusicSys`/`MUSIC_TRACKS` ‚Äî no reimplementation. New `MUSIC_LAYER_THRESHOLD = {2: 0.20, 3: 0.45, 4: 0.70}` gates off the **shipped** `difficultyFactor(game.wave)` curve, grepped and reused as instructed (no second curve). **The key design decision:** gating is a downstream **GAIN GATE**, never a scheduling omission ‚Äî `MusicSys.setState` now builds one persistent `GainNode` per layer (`this.layerGates`), sitting between each note's envelope gain and `trackGain`; `scheduleStep`/`playNote` schedule **every** layer unconditionally on every step regardless of intensity, so a layer's note timing/pitch is identical whether it's audible or not. This makes "tempo and key never change" true **by construction** ‚Äî there is no intensity branch anywhere in the scheduling path that a future edit could desync. `MusicSys.setIntensity(f)` (previously a no-op P6 stub) ramps each tier-2/3/4 gate toward 0/1 over `MUSIC_LAYER_CROSSFADE` (1.5s) via `linearRampToValueAtTime` ‚Äî a ramp, never a jump ‚Äî only when its target actually flips (reused the `setDuck` idempotency idiom); tier-1 gates are skipped entirely (bare-set to 1 once at construction, never revisited). **Called ONLY from the real `nextWave()`** (`MusicSys.setIntensity(difficultyFactor(game.wave))`, added right after `game.wave++`) ‚Äî `nextWave()` already runs once at `startGame()`, so a fresh run starts correctly pinned to `difficultyFactor(1) === 0` before any track even loads; the per-frame `updateMusic()` path is untouched, no per-frame recompute added. **(3) TRACK SELECTION ACTUALLY WIRED:** `musicStateFor(s)` now returns `settings.musicTrack` (not a generic `"play"`) when `s === "playing"` ‚Äî since the selected name IS a `MUSIC_TRACKS` key, switching tracks mid-game (Options, pause menu) falls straight out of `setState()`'s existing crossfade on the very next `updateMusic()` frame; no separate track-switch code path was needed or written. **(4) PERF (FLAG-9c, the round's explicitly flagged biggest risk) ‚Äî measured, not estimated:** since every layer is always scheduled, per-step node creation is intensity-**independent**, so "at max intensity" and "always" are the same measurement. A counting wrapper around `ctx.createGain`/`createOscillator`/`createBiquadFilter`, driven across one full loop of each track, found worst-case nodes for a single scheduled step = **7 (tense)**, **6 (retro)**, **6 (ambient)** ‚Äî **overall worst case 7**, comfortably inside the "handful" budget the prompt set; no track uses oscillator detune (which would have doubled the oscillator count), and only 2 of the 12 layers across all three tracks use a filter. All output routes into `AudioSys.music`, so the existing Music Volume slider governs it with zero new plumbing; signal path **note envelopes ‚Üí per-state `trackGain` (crossfaded) ‚Üí `MusicSys.duck` ‚Üí `AudioSys.music`**. **The scheduler** is a standard Web Audio **lookahead**: `MusicSys.update()`, called once per frame from a new `updateMusic()` in the main loop, schedules any note starting within `MUSIC_LOOKAHEAD` (0.2 s) of `ctx.currentTime`, stepping a **generic step-sequencer track table** (`{stepDur, steps, layers:[{type,gain,steps:[cell|null]}]}`) ‚Äî never `setTimeout`. `scheduleStep` clamps a note's start to `max(stepTime, currentTime)` so a stalled frame can't schedule into the past. **Tracks are DATA** (`MUSIC_TRACKS`), so P7 adds three more tables without touching the scheduler. `setState("title"|"play"|"off")` crossfades (old `trackGain` ramps to silence, new ramps in) ‚Äî driven each frame off `game.state` (`playing‚Üí"play"`, `title‚Üí"title"`, else‚Üísilence, game-over via `MUSIC_FADE_OUT` ~1 s). `setDuck(menuActive())` ramps `duck` to `MUSIC_DUCK_GAIN` (0.5) over `MUSIC_DUCK_RAMP` (0.15 s, `linearRampToValueAtTime`) while any pause screen is open (`menuActive()` ‚áî `game.paused` covers Pause/Options/Difficulty/Controls/Achievements ‚Äî one line for the whole ¬ß9 spec) and is **idempotent** (only ramps on a change; reordered so the duck node is built at its current level *before* `this.ducked` flips, so the move is always a ramp, never a jump). Every entry point is `if (!AudioSys.ctx) return;`-guarded like every `AudioSys` voice; the `duck` node is built lazily via `ensureGraph`. `setIntensity(f)` is a no-op stub (P7). **(2) TITLE TRACK** ‚Äî one long, patient, epic-adventure synthesized loop (48 s = 96 steps √ó 0.5 s) via `buildTitleTrack()`: five WebAudio layers (low sine bass drone, two detuned triangle pads at root + open fifth, an octave shimmer, a sparse high lead entering in the back half), no percussion, wide intervals, no audio files. **(3) OPTIONS REFACTOR + ROW** ‚Äî `menuOptions()`/`drawOptionsMenu()` dispatched on **hardcoded row indices**; both refactored to **dispatch by label** (the `menuRoot` precedent) as a distinct verified step, then the **Music Track** row added purely additively after "Master Volume" ‚Äî a left/right cycle over `["Tense","Retro","Ambient"]` (Difficulty-toggle idiom), rendered with a value column mirroring `drawDifficulty`. Math.max(lever.floor, ramp(lever.start, lever.floor, wave)) : lever.start` (the disabled branch skips `ramp` entirely but the `Math.max` clamp still applies, so `start` itself must never be below `floor` ‚Äî it isn't, for either lever built this phase). Reverses three shipped v3.2 rules; Paul signed off on all three (FORK-4 no [clumps don't decay], FORK-5 yes [delete `bornOfScrap`], FORK-6 no [clump-scoop unconditional]).** **9a ‚Äî SINGLE GARBAGE DECAYS AGAIN (reverses v3.2 P3):** reintroduced `GARBAGE_DECAY` (**22 s**, a new constant + `GARBAGE_FADE` **2.0** for the blink-out) on `Garbage`; it counts down in `Garbage.update()` **only while `pieces === 1`** and sets `dead` at 0, with a restored blink/fade branch in `Garbage.draw()` for the last ~2 s (skip "off" half-cycles via `sin(decay¬∑18)`, fading alpha as death nears). A **clump (`pieces > 1`) never decays** (FORK-4) ‚Äî it's a target and a scoopable pickup, so aging it out would steal loot + the Hunter-prevention window. Intentional: 9a's single-decay is the governor now (a single visible universal lever, not hidden per-lineage plumbing). `game.stats.hunterCoalesced` is still bumped once at the transform and **never read the flag**, so **Waste Not is untouched** (verified via a direct `Achievements.byId["waste_not"].cur()` assertion). **9c ‚Äî CLUMPS ARE SCOOPABLE (reverses v3.2 P1's "un-hookable"):** restructured the pickup-pass capture gate ‚Äî the region (`game.chain.length < game.cargoMax && (dist2 < pickR¬≤ || inScoopBox(g))`) now branches on `pieces`: a single hooks as one node (unchanged, incl. the magnet-budget decrement), a **clump is scooped** ‚Äî `room = cargoMax ‚àí chain.length`, `take = min(room, pieces)`, push `take` chain nodes at `(g.x,g.y)` each at `pMass = g.mass/g.pieces` (carrying `spin`/`spinRate`); if `take === pieces` the clump dies (mass conserved onto the chain), else the leftover survives with `pieces`/`mass`/`radius = 7¬∑‚àöpieces` re-derived, `coalesceDelay` re-armed to `GARBAGE_COALESCE_DELAY`, the cached P1 hull regenerated via `makeClumpHull`, and an outward **`SCOOP_SPILL_KICK`** (**85** px/s, new knob) kick directly away from the ship via wrap-aware `shortDelta` ("the rest of the ball floats off and away"). **Unconditional** ‚Äî no `scoopLevel` gate (FORK-6): the base circle scoops clumps even at scoopLevel 0, the box just makes it easy. The Magnet still ignores clumps (`pieces === 1` gate in the pull kept). A partial scoop only happens when the chain fills, so the leftover can't be immediately re-scooped ‚Äî **no cooldown added.** **Shatter (v3.2 P2) survives and keeps its purpose:** shatter is LOSSLESS (all pieces become hookable singles you can come back for), scooping is LOSSY but instant (greedily scooping a 10-clump with 3 slots throws 7 away) ‚Äî greed vs. tidiness, same fulcrum as v3.2. **Headless-tested through the REAL `update()`/`coalesceGarbage`/`destroyHunter`/pickup pass (no reimplementation):** `scratchpad/test-v31-coalesce.js` **rewritten** 80‚Üí**109 assertions** ‚Äî its `bornOfScrap`-emits-ZERO assertions (sections 17/19/20) now assert the **inverse** (a scrap-born lineage emits the full 66; `bornOfScrap` is absent from the source at every generation; the coalesced core has no such field), section 6 flipped from "clump un-hookable" to "clump scooped," section 16 flipped from "never dies of age" to "single ages out at `GARBAGE_DECAY`, clump never decays," and new sections cover: a chain node never decays + `!('decay' in node)`; `GARBAGE_DECAY > GARBAGE_COALESCE_DELAY¬∑3` (assert the RELATIONSHIP); scoop a 5-clump with room ‚Üí exactly 5 nodes at mass `clumpMass/5`, clump dead, mass conserved; a partial scoop of a 10-clump into 3 slots ‚Üí 3 nodes + a live 7-piece leftover with re-derived radius/mass, re-armed delay, regenerated hull, outward kick, and NO immediate re-scoop; scooping at `scoopLevel 0` via the circle AND (at L5) through the box; Waste Not still fires on `hunterCoalesced === 0` and not on 1. (2) `maybeDropPowerup` no longer flat-picks `POWERUP_DROP_TYPES`; it does a **weighted** roll over a new **separate** table **`POWERUP_DROP_WEIGHTS = {rapid: 3, triple: 3, scoop: 2, magnet: 1, engine: 1}`** (favors the shot powerups; weights are the knob). (3) **CRITICAL, honored:** `POWERUP_DROP_TYPES` (the list the HUD active-effect row / `powerActive`/`powerMode`/`powerBudget` iterate as the *timed* effects) was **left untouched** ‚Äî Scoop is persistent, not timed, and is **NOT** in it. The two structures are distinct (FLAG A-9). **PART B ‚Äî the Scoop (¬ß8), a PERSISTENT, non-timed ship upgrade ‚Äî the first of its kind here:** (1) **State** ‚Äî `game.scoopLevel` (0..`SCOOP_MAX_LEVEL` = **5**) + `game.scoopHits`, both reset in `startGame()` and added to the `game` literal; deliberately **NOT** in `game.powerFx`, **NOT** in `game.powerBudget`. (2) **New droppable `"scoop"`** ‚Äî its own `drawPowerupGlyph` case (a widening funnel/V), its own `POWERUP_COLOR.scoop` (**`#c07bff`** violet ‚Äî no other purple in the palette, so it's an unmistakable pickup and never reads as a hazard tell) + `POWERUP_LABEL.scoop`. `applyPowerup("scoop")` is handled in a **new early-return branch** (before the `health`/`powerMode` branches, since `powerMode("scoop")` would wrongly fall to `"time"`): raises `scoopLevel` by 1 capped at 5 (`"SCOOP +1"` float), or at the cap pays `SCOOP_MAX_BONUS` (**500**, via `addScore`) + a `"SCOOP MAX"` float ‚Äî mirroring the full-HP milestone. It increments `game.stats.powerupsPicked` (so it IS a powerup ‚Äî **freezes `maxWaveNoPowerup`**, FLAG A-8, accepted) but does **not** touch `powerUsed[]` (that gates "Powered Up", the four timed types only). (3) **Geometry ‚Äî an oriented capture BOX (the mouth):** `SCOOP_WIDTH = [0,22,30,38,46,54]` (index = level; L5 width 54 = **3√ó the drawn ship's 18 px**), `SCOOP_DEPTH = [0,20,24,28,32,36]` px forward of the ship center. A new flow helper **`inScoopBox(g)`** takes the wrap-aware `shortDelta(ship‚Üígarbage)`, projects it onto the ship's facing axis (`forward = dx¬∑cos+dy¬∑sin`) and its normal (`lateral = ‚àídx¬∑sin+dy¬∑cos`), and returns true if `|lateral| ‚â§ SCOOP_WIDTH[lvl]/2` AND `‚àíSHIP_RADIUS ‚â§ forward ‚â§ SCOOP_DEPTH[lvl]`. In the pickup pass the gate became `game.chain.length < cargoMax && g.pieces === 1 && (dist2 < pickR¬≤ || inScoopBox(g))` ‚Äî **OR'd with the base circle**, which always still applies. At `scoopLevel 0`, `inScoopBox` returns false (width/depth 0), so pickup is **byte-identical to the pre-scoop build**; `MAGNET_PICKUP_MULT` still multiplies the **circle only** (the box is level-driven, independent ‚Äî no double-count). It still only captures `pieces === 1` (clump-scooping is P4/9c, not this phase). (4) **Decay by damage** ‚Äî in `damageShip()`, after the existing HP/knockback/particles/`AudioSys.hit()` work and before the final `return true` (so only the *non-lethal* path reaches it, and the shield/hit-stun/dead early-return above means shielded/i-frame hits never count): `if (scoopLevel > 0) { scoopHits++; if (scoopHits >= SCOOP_HITS_PER_LEVEL (2)) { scoopLevel = max(0, ‚àí1); scoopHits = 0; "SCOOP ‚àí1" float; AudioSys.scooploss(); } }`. The `scoopLevel > 0` guard means hits at level 0 don't accumulate (so a fresh level isn't instantly eaten by a stale tally), scoopHits is NOT reset on a scoop pickup (FORK-3), and there is **no time decay**. (5) **New `AudioSys.scooploss()`** ‚Äî a short deflating triangle 520‚Üí180 Hz downward blip (~0.2 s), distinct from `hit`/`pickup`. (6) **Render** ‚Äî `Ship.draw()`, before the hull (inside the `!blink` block so it blinks with the ship), draws two prongs as an open `drawPoly` V `[[d,‚àíhw],[16,0],[d,hw]]` (throat at the nose (16,0), flaring forward to ¬±width/2 at the mouth depth) in `COLOR.dock` green so it reads as a collector; hidden at level 0, visibly 3√ó the ship at L5. (7) **HUD** ‚Äî a `SCOOP` 5-pip row (filled = current level, in the scoop violet) under the active-powerup rows, hidden at level 0, drawn **outside** the `POWERUP_DROP_TYPES`/`powerActive` loop (it is persistent state, not a timed bar). **Headless-tested** (`scratchpad/test-v33-p3.js`, new, **46 assertions**, driving the REAL `update()`/`damageShip()`/`applyPowerup`/`maybeDropPowerup` ‚Äî no reimplementation): constants + the two-table separation (scoop absent from `POWERUP_DROP_TYPES`, present in `POWERUP_DROP_WEIGHTS`); `applyPowerup("scoop")` climbs 0‚Üí5, caps, and pays `SCOOP_MAX_BONUS` on the 6th pick with `powerupsPicked` up 6; the box captures a canister at forward 30 (outside the 18 px circle) at **six headings** AND across **both** world wrap seams, plus a forward-25/lateral-20 in-mouth case; canisters **behind** the ship, laterally outside the mouth (lateral 40 > 27), or beyond depth (forward 80) are **not** captured; at `scoopLevel 0` a forward-30 canister is NOT captured while a forward-10 (in-circle) one IS (base behavior intact, and the exact L5 capture fails at L0); two non-lethal hits drop exactly one level and four drop two (driven through the real `damageShip`, clearing `invuln` between), hits at level 0 are harmless (no underflow); a **shielded** and an **i-frame** hit both early-return and leave `scoopHits`/`scoopLevel` untouched; 2000 `maybeDropPowerup` rolls only ever yield weighted types (scoop drops, Health never does). A render smoke (`draw()`/prongs/pips/glyph/`scooploss` at levels 0/3/5 with a full powerup HUD row) is crash-free. **Full regression re-run green: all 21 test files, 962 assertions** (up from 916 ‚Äî the new file adds 46; **no existing test needed a change**, confirming the additive scope held). `node --check` clean on the extracted script.
